- ADHD pre-release audit and `force_disconnect` fixes (2026-06-02, **BUILD OK / HW PENDING**): completed a deep "ADHD" methodology audit focusing on string bounds, memory aliasing (`overlay_slot`/`rx_line`), and ABI safety (`irc_send_cmd_internal`). Verified `st_copy_n` correctly caps limits project-wide. Verified the `SPCTLK2` (ABOUT) overlay safely isolates its animation data using `_about_packet_slot` to prevent clobbering the UART's `rx_line`. Verified that `__z88dk_callee` and ASM wrappers (`irc_send_cmd1`, `irc_send_cmd2`) correctly preserve `IX`/`IY` and restore the stack layout without leaks. Found and fixed a state leak in `force_disconnect()` in `src/spectalk.c` where `ping_latency`, `post_cancel_quiet`, `count_sync_idle_frames`, and `count_sync_quits` were not reset on disconnect, leading to ghost states upon reconnection. Build: TAP `36054B` (`+14B` for resets), BSS guard `0xF2CE < 0xF500` (`562B` free), overlays `1704/1774/1944/1750/1902/1651/1834/1884` (unchanged), `SPECTALK.OVL=14507B` (unchanged).

- STATUS defer on PLF rejected (2026-05-27, **USER REJECTED / BRANCH DELETED**): isolated branch `codex/status-defer-on-plf-proto` stacked on the HW OK PLF candidate tested delaying `draw_status_bar_real()` while `rx_pos != 0 || rb_head != rb_tail`. - PUTS PLF lift prototype (2026-05-27, **BUILD OK / HW OK**): opened isolated worktree `experimentos/puts-plf-lift-proto` on branch `codex/puts-plf-lift-proto` to test Claude's `PUTS-PLF-LIFT` idea without any debug/border/perf code. `_main_puts` now has a guarded fast path before BPE setup: only even `main_col`, non-empty ASCII strings of at least 4 bytes, no BPE token (`>=0x80`), no newline/control, and full fit within the current 64-col row. Accepted chunks render through existing `_print_line64_fast` with bounded `plf_pair_count`, then update `main_col`; all odd-column, wrapping, BPE, newline, control, short, and overlay cases fall through to the old per-char path. This targets common mid-line IRC chunks such as nicks/text after the timestamp without changing semantics intentionally. Rejected from the same Claude batch for now: `RING-ROW` is not a simple safe win on ZX bitmap because visible scanout order cannot be remapped without a backing text buffer or full repaint, `DRAIN-IN-SCROLL` already produced the HW "under water" scroll rejection, and `VERB-FASTPATH` is mostly already captured by the hot-first `CMD_TABLE`. Build metrics: TAP `35881B` (`+85B` vs branch baseline `35796B`), BSS guard `0xF3D7 < 0xF500` (`297B` free), overlays `1704/1774/1961/1750/1902/1651/1834/1884`, packed `SPECTALK.OVL=16384B`. Verification: `git diff --check` passed (CRLF warning only) and `make NO_COLOR=1` passed. HW result: user reports the candidate looks good; no visible corruption or wrap/BPE regression reported in the smoke pass. Candidate is promotable if the +85B resident cost is accepted for smoother normal text rendering.
- UART scroll-poll worktree rejected (2026-05-27, **HW REJECTED / BRANCH DELETED**): isolated branch `codex/uart-scroll-poll-proto` in `experimentos/uart-scroll-poll` tested one `_uart_drain_to_buffer` call per `_scroll_main_zone` bitmap scanline, placed only after stack-blit blocks where `SP` was restored. Build passed with TAP `35796B`, BSS guard `0xF382 < 0xF500` (`382B` free), overlays `1704/1774/1961/1750/1902/1651/1834/1884`, but HW/user perception rejected it: scroll felt irregular, "under water", consistent with variable per-scanline UART drain cost. Do not retry scanline-level drain in visible scroll unless it is strictly bounded to near-constant time or decoupled from the visual scroll cadence.
- NAMES friend initial-gate retry (2026-05-27, **BUILD OK / HW OK modest gain**): second, narrower attempt after the full NAMES friend-scan ASM regression. Kept the existing C tokenization and notification append logic, kept `notif_buf`/`names_friend_pos` static, and added only resident ASM `friend_initial_match(char)` to test whether a NAMES nick's first folded byte can match any configured friend before mutating the token and calling the heavier `is_tracked_friend()`. This avoids most per-nick temporary NUL writes and `is_tracked_friend()` calls when friends are configured, without changing count semantics or 366 timing. Build metrics: TAP `35814B` (`+21B` vs restored bookmark/BPE candidate), BSS guard `0xF394 < 0xF500` (`364B` free), overlays `1704/1774/1961/1750/1902/1651/1834/1884`, packed `SPECTALK.OVL=16384B`. HW result: user reports the improvement is perceptible; keep as modest, transparent latency win unless later connect/NAMES regressions appear.
- NAMES friend-scan ASM rejected (2026-05-27, **HW REJECTED / REVERTED**): tried the SAFE-looking Gemini NAMES latency option that moved the cosmetic NAMES friend accumulator from the C loop in `h_numeric_353()` to resident ASM `_names_accum_friends`, preserving exact count behavior, 366 commit timing, friend guards, prefix skipping, delimiter restore, and the 46-character notification cap. Build passed and shrank TAP to `35710B` with BSS guard `0xF32C < 0xF500`, but HW immediately showed a connection regression before channel/NAMES benefit could be evaluated: connecting to a server became much slower / timed out more often after `AT+CIPSTART OK`, with server-close/retry timeout behavior. Reverted completely to the previous bookmark/BPE candidate. - Bookmark channel contamination fix (2026-05-27, **BUILD OK / HW PENDING**): fixed the reported `!bm` regression where loading one bookmark could connect to that bookmark's server but replay channels from another bookmark. Root cause: `bookmark_save_current()` used `snapshot_autojoin_channels()` and then copied scratch `search_pattern` into global `autojoin_channels`; when not fully IRC-ready, that snapshot intentionally preserved stale `search_pattern` for normal config saves, which is wrong for per-slot bookmark storage. `S:STORE` now clears `search_pattern` when below `STATE_IRC_READY`, snapshots live joined channels only when available, and `bookmarks_save_ovl()` writes the bookmark channel field from scratch `search_pattern` instead of mutating/saving global `autojoin_channels`. Behavior note: storing a bookmark while disconnected now writes no channels unless a live IRC channel snapshot exists; store while joined to capture channels. Existing already-corrupted bookmark files must be re-stored once. Build metrics: TAP `35793B`, BSS guard `0xF37F < 0xF500` (`385B` free), overlays `1704/1774/1961/1750/1902/1651/1834/1884`, packed `SPECTALK.OVL=16384B`.
- BPE/raw overlay audit fix (2026-05-27, **BUILD OK / HW PENDING**): `audit-z80` found a PROVEN regression in the resident-string import shrink: BPE-compressed `SB_*` strings had leaked into raw consumers. `overlay/local_cmds_ovl.c` now uses raw literals again for `st_stricmp()` option parsing (`on`, `off`, `smart`), while keeping `SB_*` only on BPE-aware output paths (`main_print`, `sys_puts_print`, `ui_err`). `overlay/spectalk_ovl5.c` restored local raw `cv_*` constants for direct `print_str64()` config rendering. `overlay/overlay_api.h` and `tools/gen_overlay_defs.py` removed the unsafe unused `SB_NOTSET`/`SB_SET` exports. Verification: code search found no `st_stricmp(...SB_)`, no direct-render `print_str64`/`print_line64_fast`/`print_big_str` with `SB_*`, and no remaining `SB_NOTSET`/`SB_SET` overlay references. Build metrics after fix: TAP `35796B`, BSS guard `0xF382 < 0xF500` (`382B` free), overlays `1704/1774/1961/1750/1902/1651/1834/1884`, packed `SPECTALK.OVL=16384B`. Cost vs broken shrink build: `SPCTLK5 +27B`, `SPCTLK7 +24B`; net vs pre-import baseline still `SPCTLK1 -7B`, `SPCTLK5 -6B`, `SPCTLK7 -33B`.

- Bookmarks autosave/autoconnect state follow-up (2026-05-18, **BUILD OK / HW PENDING**): bookmark changes now persist to SD immediately. `S:STORE` writes the selected slot file from the current server/port/server password/current non-query channels and shows `OK`; if that slot is the active autoconnect bookmark it also saves config immediately. `A:AUTO` cycles selected slot through no marker -> autoconnect-only -> autologin -> off, saves config immediately, and uses `c`/`o` markers as the current 64-col-safe half/full circle fallback. `D:DELETE` truncates the slot file and, if it was active, clears `autoconnect`, `autojoin`, the saved channel CSV, and saves config immediately. `ENTER` still loads the slot for a manual connect without changing persistent autoconnect state. `!config` now shows only `autoconnect=` and `autologin=` for this area; `channels=` remains saved internally but is not displayed. Config no longer writes a separate bookmark slot key: boot behavior persists through the normal `server`/`port`/`pass`/`autoconnect`/`autojoin`/`channels` fields, and `SPCTLK8` reconstructs the visible marker when opened by matching the configured server to a bookmark slot while autoconnect is enabled. `cmd_save()` skips live channel resnapshot while the bookmarks overlay is active, so bookmark-triggered config saves preserve the selected bookmark's stored channel list rather than the currently open windows. `!autoconnect off` now clears bookmark autoconnect/autologin state; `!autojoin on` implies autoconnect and upgrades an active bookmark to autologin, while `!autojoin off` downgrades it to autoconnect-only. Error strings in the cold bookmark store overlay were collapsed to `Error` and the optional no-port fallback was removed to fit. Verification: `git diff --check` passed (CRLF warnings only) and `make NO_COLOR=1` passed: TAP `36151B`, BSS guard `0xF4E5 < 0xF500` (`27B` free), overlays `1711/1774/2031/1934/1908/1651/1956/2048`, packed `SPECTALK.OVL=16384B`. Margin is now extremely tight: resident `27B` free and `SPCTLK8.OVL` exactly `2048B`; no further bookmark UI polish should be added without first freeing bytes. HW checks still needed: SD autosave after `S`/`A`/`D`, autoconnect-only boot, autologin boot with channels, active marker reconstruction after reboot, query windows excluded from saved CSV, long wrapped channel lists, server password restore, connected-load confirm/cancel/no input echo, and normal `!config`/What's New behavior.
- Bookmarks overlay MVP worktree (2026-05-18, **BUILD OK / HW PENDING**): created isolated worktree `experimentos/bookmarks-overlay` on branch `codex/bookmarks-overlay` from `main` commit `0d66a67`. Baseline build in this clean worktree passed after copying ignored `src/SPECTALK.DAT` from the main checkout: TAP `35589B`, BSS guard `0xF2AC < 0xF500` (`596B` free), overlays `1711/1774/1253/1911/1941/1651/1898`, packed `SPECTALK.OVL=14336B`. Implemented zero-table IRC bookmarks through a split overlay design: `SPCTLK8.OVL` renders/moves the selector and deletes slots, while `SPCTLK3.OVL` uses spare What's New space for cold load/save/apply entries. `!bookmarks`/`!bm` opens exactly five user slots, `UP/DOWN` repaints only the previous/current server rows without clearing them, `ENTER` loads the selected bookmark and starts the existing `/server` reconnect path, `S` snapshots current active non-query IRC channel slots into `autojoin_channels`, saves current server/port/server-pass/channels, and repaints only the list area, `A` toggles selected-bookmark autojoin on/off (`on` applies the bookmark with `autojoin=1`, `off` clears `autojoin` and the marker) and repaints only affected server marker rows, `D` deletes the selected slot by truncating its bookmark file and repaints the list, and `BREAK` exits. User slots are file-backed as `/SYS/CONFIG/SPTBM1.CFG`..`SPTBM5.CFG` with compact `server|port|pass|channels` records; compiled defaults were removed. Header is left-aligned double-height `BOOKMARKS`; footer is the Ikkle line `ENTER:CONNECT  S:SAVE  A:AUTOJOIN  D:DELETE  BREAK:EXIT`; active autojoin marker is `*`; occupied server rows use yellow (`theme_attrs[10]`) and selected rows use bright attribute; channel rows stay cyan. List rows start at row 6 and channel lists wrap on comma/space below the server name, while preserving at least one visible row per remaining bookmark. Server passwords (`/pass`, third bookmark field) are saved/restored and shown only as `P`; NickServ password stays global config (`nickpass=`/`/id` path), not per-bookmark because the current resident guard and `SPCTLK3` budget are too tight for a compatible fifth-field implementation without more shrink/split work. `!config` no longer renders `channels=` because bookmarks expose the channel list, while the existing autojoin config path remains. Saving a bookmark no longer marks it as active autojoin; `A` is now the only autojoin marker toggle. `!autojoin off` clears the active bookmark marker. The shared yes/no prompt now waits for key release so `Disconnect (y/n)?` answers are not echoed into user input. Active-slot state is resident/session-local; persist resulting config with `!save` if it should survive reboot. `git diff --check` passed (CRLF warnings only) and `make NO_COLOR=1` passed: TAP `36069B` (`+480B` vs baseline), BSS guard `0xF493 < 0xF500` (`109B` free, `-487B`), overlays `1711/1774/2024/1911/1897/1651/1908/1991`, packed `SPECTALK.OVL=16384B` (`8 x 2048`). - Overlay seek F_SEEK wrapper shrink (2026-05-18, **BUILD OK / HW PENDING**): `ovl_seek_block` no longer duplicates the esxDOS `F_SEEK` sequence. It computes `HL = ovl_id * 2048` and tail-jumps to `_esx_fseek_set`, which already preserves `IX/IY` and leaves Carry reflecting the esxDOS result because `sbc hl,hl / inc hl` does not destroy Carry. - esxDOS F_SEEK IY preservation audit fix (2026-05-17, **BUILD OK / HW PENDING**): accepted Claude W01/W02 only. `_esx_fseek_set` and `ovl_seek_block` now preserve `IY` across `RST 8 / F_SEEK`, matching the other esxDOS wrappers and the `sdcc_iy` runtime contract. `push/pop iy` does not alter Carry, so `_esx_fseek_set` keeps its `sbc hl,hl / inc hl` return contract and overlay seek still branches on the esxDOS Carry result. - `/msg` existing-query pointer lifetime fix (2026-05-17, **BUILD OK / HW PENDING**): fixed the audit-proven regression from the query-divider semantics change. `cmd_msg()` had moved `switch_to_channel()` before `irc_send_privmsg()` for existing private queries, but `target/msg` still pointed into `temp_input`; `switch_to_channel()` draws the divider through `channel_context_banner()`, which also uses `temp_input`, so the outgoing target/text could be clobbered before send/echo. The fix copies `msg` into `line_buffer` before switching, then sends to the now-current `irc_channel` with the preserved text and clears `line_buffer[0]` to keep the empty-input/history invariant. Missing-query `/msg` still stays in the current context and does not create a divider. `git diff --check` passed (CRLF warnings only) and `make NO_COLOR=1` passed: TAP `35599B`, BSS guard `0xF2B6 < 0xF500` (`586B` free), overlays `1711/1774/1253/1911/1941/1651/1898`, packed `SPECTALK.OVL=14336B`. - UART P02 `_is_recv` latch removal accepted (2026-05-15, **HW OK by user**): removed the software RX-ready latch from `asm/divmmc_uart.asm`; `uartRead` now always checks the hardware status bit before reading DATA, and `_ay_uart_send` only selects/polls the status register for TX-ready. Build passed: TAP `35444B` (`-26B` vs diagnostic probe base), BSS guard `0xF224 < 0xF500` (`732B` free), overlays unchanged `1711/1774/1253/1895/1917/1651/1852`, packed `SPECTALK.OVL=14336B`. `rg` confirmed `_is_recv` absent from sources and map. - UART P01 fast resident drain rejected and reverted (2026-05-15, **HW REJECTED by user**): the inline `_uart_drain_to_buffer` build (`5d2958b`) booted but made the whole client very slow. Diagnostic showed `calls 9180`, `bytes 9003`, `max/call 1`, `empty 178`, `limit-hit 0`, `ring-full 0`, `ring-now 0`, `rxov/press 0/0`, plus a visible typo-driven `Unknown command: !aurtdiag`. This proves the implementation did not lose bytes, but it rechecked RX status immediately after each DATA read and usually exited before the next serial byte had physically arrived, degrading drains to one byte per call. Reverted in `05bc593`; keep P02 as the current HW-good UART candidate. Future fast-drain attempts need a bounded post-byte settle/retry window or a caller-side loop that does not collapse to one byte per drain.
- UART Package 1 / P1A safe-push rejected and reverted (2026-05-15, **HW REJECTED by user**): the package kept `call uartRead` but cached `rb_head`, inlined `_rb_push`, and wrote `rb_head` once at drain exit. Build had passed as TAP `35486B` (`+42B` vs P02), but HW showed the same user-visible regression as P01: server/MOTD messages advanced at roughly one line every 2-3 seconds. Reverted in `14c3802`; current worktree returns to P02 + diagnostic probe. Lesson: do not defer `rb_head` publication across the whole drain in this runtime; any next RX experiment must preserve per-byte head publication or move to scheduler/wait-loop work.
- UART Package 2 / P2W broad wait-drain rejected and reverted (2026-05-15, **HW REJECTED by user**): broad `_frame_wait_drain` integration kept UX responsive but made `/names` often incomplete. Diagnostics showed `ring-full` non-zero during paginated `/names` (about `353` in `#madrid` and `82` in `#linux`) with `rxov/press 0/0`, proving the issue was aggressive background draining into the ring while pagination intentionally stopped parsing. Reverted in `9c649a4`. Lesson: do not use busy frame-wait draining inside `pagination_pause`; it fills the ring faster than the paused consumer can process.
- UART Package 2-lite / P2WL wait-drain accepted (2026-05-15, **HW OK by user**): reintroduced resident-only `_frame_wait_drain`, but excluded pagination pauses. It is used only for connection/AT waits, IRC registration wait, yes/no prompt, and init retry key waits. `!uartdiag` labels this TAP as `UART diag P2WL`. Build passed: TAP `35444B` (same as P02/probe base), BSS guard `0xF224 < 0xF500` (`732B` free), overlays unchanged `1711/1774/1253/1895/1917/1651/1852`, packed `SPECTALK.OVL=14336B`; cleanup left `build/SPCTLK7.OVL` locked once but the file was removed manually afterward. User reports connection/MOTD responsiveness improved and appreciable. Current UART lab candidate is P02 + P2WL + diagnostic probe.
- UART Package 3 / P3TX opportunistic RX during TX wait tested (2026-05-15, **HW OK but MARGINAL**): `_ay_uart_send` now drains at most one pending RX byte while it is already waiting for TX-ready, then restores the UART status-register selection before sending. Diagnostic label changes to `UART diag P3TX` and adds `txrx`, the count of RX bytes successfully moved to the ring from the TX wait loop. Expected gain is bidirectional reliability only: reduced ESP FIFO pressure when the Spectrum is sending while the server is also sending. It should not materially accelerate receive-only `/names`; if `txrx` remains near zero in real sessions, the package has no practical value and should be reverted. Build passed: TAP `35514B` (`+70B` vs P2WL), BSS guard `0xF26C < 0xF500` (`660B` free), overlays unchanged `1711/1774/1253/1895/1917/1651/1852`, packed `SPECTALK.OVL=14336B`. HW diagnostics: Chathispano `#madrid` `[472 listed]`: calls `651`, bytes `8228`, txrx `14`, max/call `255`, empty `406`, limit-hit `235`, ring-full `0`, ring-now `0`, rxov/press `0/0`; Libera `#linux` `[2460 listed]`: calls `1058`, bytes `22768`, txrx `0`, max/call `32`, empty `346`, limit-hit `711`, ring-full `0`, ring-now `0`, rxov/press `0/0`. Safety signal is good, but practical gain is tiny (`0.17%` of bytes in Madrid and `0%` in Linux); do not promote unless later bidirectional tests show higher `txrx`.
- UART Package 4 / P4RX settled RX drain rejected and reverted (2026-05-15, **HW REJECTED: no gain**): the package added two short post-byte settle retries in `_uart_drain_to_buffer` and a `settle` counter. Build passed as TAP `35572B` (`+58B` vs P3TX, `+128B` vs P2WL), BSS guard `0xF2A8 < 0xF500` (`600B` free). HW diagnostics showed `settle=0` in both tested networks while safety stayed good: Chathispano test: calls `637`, bytes `7312`, txrx `0`, settle `0`, max/call `255`, limit-hit `217`, ring-full `0`, ring-now `0`, rxov/press `0/0`; Libera `#linux` `[2472 listed]`: calls `1029`, bytes `22934`, txrx `0`, settle `0`, max/call `32`, empty `316`, limit-hit `716`, ring-full `0`, ring-now `0`, rxov/press `0/0`. Since the added wait never captured extra bytes, it was pure resident cost/CPU delay. Reverted in the next commit; current code returns to P3TX.
- UART Package 5 / P5RD inline drain read rejected and reverted (2026-05-15, **HW REJECTED by user**): `_uart_drain_to_buffer` inlined the UART status/DATA read while still calling `_rb_push` per byte. Build passed as TAP `35531B` (`+17B` vs P3TX, `+87B` vs P2WL), BSS guard `0xF27D < 0xF500` (`643B` free). HW report: same visible regression as P01/P1A, server output advancing roughly one line every 2-3 seconds. Reverted immediately; current code returns to P3TX. Lesson: even partial inlining of the read path changes timing badly on real hardware, probably by rechecking RX status too tightly after each DATA read. Do not retry drain-loop register inlining without an explicit hardware-timed pacing design.
- UART Package 6 / P6BQ transient ESP baud probe rejected and reverted (2026-05-15, **HW REJECTED: one-sided baud change**): `!uartbaud` confirmed the ESP supports `AT+UART_CUR?`, reporting `+UART_CUR:115273,8,1,0,2` on this module. `!uartbaud 230400` returned `OK`, proving `AT+UART_CUR=230400,8,1,0,0` is accepted transiently by the ESP, but afterwards the client could not connect because the Spectrum-side UART remained at the fixed ZX-Uno-compatible 115200 DATA/STAT interface. This path is not useful without a known Spectrum-side baud divisor/register. The lab command was large (`+407B` vs P3TX, BSS slack down to `253B`) and was reverted; keep the hardware result as evidence only.
- UART Package 7 / P7RD timed inline read rejected (2026-05-15, **HW REJECTED by user**): revisited the P5 inline UART read regression but preserved `uartRead`'s STATUS-to-DATA timing shape by reloading `BC=$FC3B` before selecting DATA instead of using the faster `DEC B` shortcut. It still called `_rb_push` per byte. Build passed as TAP `35533B` (`+19B` vs P3TX, `+89B` vs P2WL), BSS guard `0xF27F < 0xF500` (`641B` free), but HW showed the same visible regression: server output advanced roughly one line every 2-3 seconds. This rules out the `DEC B` shortcut as the main cause; the likely cause is the inline drain re-polling RX too early after a successful byte and collapsing nonempty drains to one byte per call.
- UART Package 8 / P8DW inter-byte dwell tested (2026-05-15, **HW PARTIAL OK / NOT PROMOTABLE**): keeps P7's inline UART read but adds a bounded dwell only after a drain call has already moved at least one byte. On a post-byte no-data status, it polls RX up to five short loops (about one 115200-baud byte time) before exiting, then continues the same drain if a byte appears. Diagnostic label changes to `UART diag P8DW` and adds `wait-hit`, counting bytes recovered by this dwell path. Build passed: TAP `35597B` (`+64B` vs P7RD, `+83B` vs P3TX, `+153B` vs P2WL), BSS guard `0xF2C1 < 0xF500` (`575B` free), overlays unchanged `1711/1774/1253/1895/1917/1651/1852`, packed `SPECTALK.OVL=14336B`. HW proved the core hypothesis: Chathispano `#madrid` `[568 listed]`: calls `608`, bytes `9344`, txrx `0`, wait-hit `9063`, max/call `255`, empty `327`, limit-hit `273`, ring-full `0`, ring-now `0`, rxov/press `0/0`; Libera `#linux` `[2453 listed]`: calls `1120`, bytes `23400`, txrx `0`, wait-hit `22746`, max/call `32`, empty `385`, limit-hit `733`, ring-full `3`, ring-now `0`, rxov/press `0/0`. Verdict: the one-line-every-2-3s regression is solved by inter-byte dwell, but `ring-full=3` on a large NAMES burst means this exact dwell is too aggressive for promotion. Next attempt should shorten the dwell window and keep `wait-hit`/`ring-full` as the accept/reject metrics.
- UART Package 9 / P9D3 shorter dwell accepted as first serious candidate (2026-05-15, **HW OK by user**): same design as P8DW but cuts the post-byte dwell from five status polls to three. Build passed: TAP `35597B` (same as P8DW), BSS guard `0xF2C1 < 0xF500` (`575B` free), overlays unchanged `1711/1774/1253/1895/1917/1651/1852`, packed `SPECTALK.OVL=14336B`. HW kept visible output smooth and returned all safety counters to zero: Chathispano `#madrid` `[568 listed]`: calls `790`, bytes `9273`, txrx `0`, wait-hit `8979`, max/call `32`, empty `496`, limit-hit `281`, ring-full `0`, ring-now `0`, rxov/press `0/0`; Libera `#linux` `[2512 listed]`: calls `1066`, bytes `23272`, txrx `0`, wait-hit `22544`, max/call `32`, empty `330`, limit-hit `727`, ring-full `0`, ring-now `0`, rxov/press `0/0`. Verdict: P9 fixes the P5/P7 one-byte-per-drain collapse without ring overflow in the two stress channels. Since `txrx=0` in both P9 runs and was already marginal in P3TX, the next cleanup is to remove the TX-wait opportunistic drain and keep only P9's RX drain improvement.

- UART P11D2 port-toggle micro-optimization (2026-05-15, **HW PENDING**): applied Gemini audit suggestion in `_uart_drain_to_buffer`. The DATA-register setup now uses `dec b` instead of reloading `BC=$FC3B` when entering `drain_read_ready`, and the two-poll dwell loop hoists `ld bc,DRAIN_ZXUNO_ADDR` outside the loop, restores `B` with `dec b` on failed polls, and jumps directly to `drain_read_ready` on hit. Stack/ABI contract unchanged; both entry paths reach `drain_read_ready` immediately after a STATUS read with `B=$FD` and no intervening call/clobber. `git diff --check` passed (CRLF warnings only). Build passed: TAP `34996B` (`-3B` vs lean P11D2 without diag, `+15B` vs UART lab baseline `34981B`), BSS guard `0xF058 < 0xF500` (`1192B` free), overlays unchanged `1711/1774/1253/1895/1917/1651/1852`, packed `SPECTALK.OVL=14336B`. Expected runtime effect is tiny but hot-path real: about `-6T` per successful DATA select and `-6T` per failed dwell poll. Needs light HW smoke on connect/MOTD and `/names #madrid` + `/names #linux`; there is no `!uartdiag` proof surface anymore.
- UART RX benchmark harness added (2026-05-16, **HW PENDING / LAB-ONLY**): added hidden `!rxbench [reset]` to quantify each future optimization before/after without treating `/names` speed as the objective. Counters: drain calls, empty drains, drain-limit hits, ring-full exits, parsed lines, parsed bytes, max ring backlog, manual-NAMES elapsed frames, current `rx_overflow`, and `search_data_lost`. Hot-loop overhead is intentionally limited: no per-byte counter inside `_uart_drain_to_buffer`; only per-call/empty/limit/full events are counted. Usage: `!rxbench reset`, run a fixed test (connect/MOTD, normal traffic burst, `/names #madrid`, `/names #linux`), then `!rxbench`; compare `max backlog`, `ring full`, `limit hits`, `lines/bytes`, and `names frames` against the same harness after each single optimization. `git diff --check` passed (CRLF warnings only). Build passed: TAP `35497B`, BSS guard `0xF25D < 0xF500` (`675B` free), overlays unchanged `1711/1774/1253/1895/1917/1651/1852`, packed `SPECTALK.OVL=14336B`. This is measurement scaffolding only and should be removed before any release/promote path.

- UART scheduler byte-budget scaling experiment rejected/reverted (2026-05-16, **HW REJECTED: higher pressure**): `process_irc_data()` briefly computed `current_budget` once after backlog measurement and scaled it with `max_lines` (`x4` above 1024B backlog, `x3` above 512B, `x2` above 256B). Because the objective is transmission reliability and buffer pressure, not only elapsed frames, the byte-budget scaling is not worth `+72B` and was reverted to the harness baseline scheduler.
- UART NAMES render-row drain experiment rejected/reverted (2026-05-16, **HW REJECTED by user**): `names_render_grid()` briefly called `_uart_drain_to_buffer` after each printed 4-cell row (`nrg_flush`, after `_main_newline`). Build passed: TAP `35500B` (`+3B` vs benchmark harness), BSS guard `0xF260 < 0xF500` (`672B` free). HW was worse without needing numeric capture: `/names #linux` often became incomplete. This confirms the expected risk: draining during visible NAMES rendering moves bytes from the ESP into the 2KB ring faster than the paginated/rendering consumer can keep up. Reverted; do not reintroduce row-level drains in manual NAMES render.
- UART partial-line refill experiment (2026-05-16, **HW PENDING**): `process_irc_data()` now does bounded cooperative refills only when `try_read_line_nodrain()` returns no complete line while `rx_pos != 0`. It drains up to 8 additional times without a key held, or 2 with a key held, stopping if `rb_head` does not change or `deferred_wrap_active` is set. This targets the specific partial-line case where the old scheduler could leave a long IRC line limited to one `DRAIN_NORMAL=32` drain per main-loop tick. It does not alter complete-line parse budgets, pagination waits, UART timing, render paths, overlays, or `/names` UX. `git diff --check` passed (CRLF warnings only). Build passed: TAP `35638B` (`+141B` vs benchmark harness), BSS guard `0xF2EA < 0xF500` (`534B` free), overlays unchanged `1711/1774/1253/1895/1917/1651/1852`, packed `SPECTALK.OVL=14336B`. This is expensive; accept only if HW stays loss-free and improves pressure/frames clearly enough to justify later size work.

- Keepalive false-timeout guard in channel-context experiment (2026-05-08, **HW PENDING**): hardware showed local `Connection timeout (no response)` while the session had recent visible IRC traffic. - UTF-8 decoder stack-balance fix (2026-05-08, **HW RETEST NEEDED**): source review after the long unattended freeze found the likely hard-hang root in `_utf8_to_ascii()`, not in the reverted off-channel notification handlers. `u8a_first_cont_or_latin1` was called as a helper but jumped directly to `u8a_c3` on malformed/truncated C4-FF leads, leaving the helper return address on the stack; a later `u8a_done` would pop that return address as the saved input pointer and return through corrupted stack state. Fixed by routing invalid/truncated fallback through a local label that discards the helper return (`pop af`) before `jp u8a_c3`; valid continuation still returns normally. - UTF-8 tolerant display decoder (2026-05-08, **HW PENDING**): `_utf8_to_ascii()` now preserves the first non-continuation byte after malformed multi-byte UTF-8 instead of consuming visible text, fixing the observed `dir?que no` shape into `dir? que no` when a client/server drops the `A1` continuation from `C3 A1`. It also falls back through the existing C0-FF display table for single-byte Latin-1 accent bytes from old/misconfigured IRC clients (`E1/F1/FA/...`), while valid `C2/C3` UTF-8 Latin-1 and `E2 80` smart-quote handling stay supported. Deliberate boundary: a missing UTF-8 continuation cannot be reconstructed as `á`, so broken `C3 20` remains `? ` rather than invented text. - Tagged PRIVMSG leak follow-up (2026-05-05): hardware still showed server-time/tagged channel messages such as `>> @time=... :nick!user@host PRIVMSG #chan :text` leaking as raw `PRIVMSG #chan ...` output, sometimes while another channel was active. Tightened `parse_irc_message()` line-start cleanup from one fixed whitespace/`>`/`@tags` pass into a bounded loop that repeatedly skips leading control/space tokens, ESP/raw `>` marker tokens, and IRCv3 `@tags` tokens until the real prefix/command starts. `h_privmsg_notice()` keeps the optimized hot path: for valid IRC `PRIVMSG #target :text` / `NOTICE target :text`, trailing isolation has already NUL-terminated `pkt_par` at the target, so the handler uses `pkt_par` directly and does not force lazy tokenization. It also hardens channel-targeted messages whose `#target` cannot map to an active channel: return instead of falling through to render in the current window. Rejected variants: `irc_param(0)` fixed the same target contract but forced full param tokenization on hot PRIVMSG/NOTICE and built at TAP `35296B`; direct `irc_params_ensure()`/`irc_params[0]` grew to `37770B`; local no-trailing split/param fallback shapes grew to `35348B`/`35354B`. - Prefix split + nick isolation experiment (2026-05-05, branch `codex/irc-parser-improve`, path `C:\tmp\SpecTalkZX-notif-stack-clear`, **HW PENDING**): tested the first remaining parser micro-pickup after lazy tokenization. The old prefix path did `split_next_param(pkt_usr)` and then walked the already-isolated prefix again in `isolate_nick()` to cut `nick!user@host` at `!`. It is now a single local naked ASM helper, `split_prefix_nick()`, that scans the IRC prefix once, writes NUL at the first `!`, continues to the first byte `<33`, and jumps into `split_next_param()`'s separator-skip tail to return the command start. This preserves server-prefix and nick-prefix behavior while avoiding the second prefix walk on every prefixed IRC line. Rejected shapes during measurement: a fully duplicated separator-skip helper built at TAP `35211B`; a compact tail-reuse shape with a separate post-`!` scan built at `35198B`. Final unified-loop shape verified with `git diff --check` and `make NO_COLOR=1`: TAP `35191B` (`-4B` versus lazy-tokenizer baseline `35195B`), BSS guard `0xF117 < 0xF500` (`1001B` free, `+4B`), overlays unchanged `1808/1846/1547/1992/2001/1733`; `SPECTALK.OVL=12288B`.
- Lazy IRC param tokenization experiment (2026-05-05, branch `codex/irc-parser-improve`, path `C:\tmp\SpecTalkZX-notif-stack-clear`, **HW OK**): after the fastcall/narrow tokenizer was HW OK, tested the safer central variant of Claude's "defer tokenization" idea. `parse_irc_message()` no longer tokenizes every line immediately; it marks params dirty after trailing-text isolation. `irc_param()` now calls `irc_params_ensure()` on demand, so handlers that need tokenized params get the old in-place split before reading them. `h_join()` now reads `irc_param(0)` to preserve IRCv3 extended-join behavior (`JOIN #chan account :realname`), which was the main trap in the external audit because JOIN does not visibly call `irc_param()` in the old code but still relied on `pkt_par` being split. Direct `irc_params[]` loops in `h_numeric_5()` and `h_numeric_default()` call `irc_params_ensure()` before reading the array. This keeps raw-param handlers such as `h_cap()` un-tokenized and skips the param walk for hot PRIVMSG/NOTICE/PING/PONG/QUIT/NICK/ERROR/MOTD-style lines. Build cost versus the HW-OK narrow tokenizer is `+28B` TAP and `-29B` BSS slack, but still `-30B` versus main after notifications. Verified `make NO_COLOR=1`: TAP `35195B`, BSS guard `0xF11B < 0xF500` (`997B` free), overlays unchanged `1808/1846/1547/1992/2001/1733`; `SPECTALK.OVL=12288B`. Rejected micro-probes in this shape: inlining `irc_params_ensure()` into `irc_param()` grew to TAP `35197B`; a naked ASM ensure helper grew to `35196B`. User hardware test reported all checked IRC paths working and a very large perceived speedup, so keep lazy tokenization for promotion.
- Rejected Gemini `switch(cmd_id)` dispatcher (2026-05-05, branch `codex/irc-parser-improve`): measured the proposed removal of `CMD_TABLE` in favor of a large C `switch` over `cmd_id`, preserving the same handlers and fallback logic. SDCC/z88dk did not produce the claimed compact O(logN)/jump-table win in this layout: TAP grew from the lazy-tokenizer baseline `35195B` to `35566B` (`+371B`) and BSS free dropped from `997B` to `626B`, with overlays unchanged. The change was reverted; keep the current hot-ordered `CMD_TABLE` linear dispatch unless a hand-written dispatcher or much smaller command set is measured separately.
- IRC param tokenizer fastcall/narrowing experiment (2026-05-05, branch `codex/irc-parser-improve`, path `C:\tmp\SpecTalkZX-notif-stack-clear`, **HW OK**): focused on the hot parser tokenization path without changing dispatch, RX drain, `/names`, fallback rendering, or text sanitization contracts. `tokenize_params()` now has the real single-callsite ABI `void tokenize_params(char *par) __z88dk_fastcall`; the old `max_params` argument and default/clamp logic were dead because `parse_irc_message()` always passed `0` for the default 10 slots. The ASM tokenizer now uses fixed `B=10`, tracks `_irc_param_count` as `10-B` once at exit instead of loading/storing the global per token, uses `DE` as the `_irc_params` write cursor instead of costly `IY` offsets/preserve, and removes tokenizer-local leading space/colon and NULL-pointer guards that are already guaranteed by `split_next_param()` plus trailing-text isolation. `irc_param()` also drops its dead internal `!irc_params[idx]` check because `idx < irc_param_count` implies the tokenizer wrote a non-NULL token pointer. Rejected during this pass: removing `parse_irc_message()`'s `!line` check; although logically tempting, the build jumped to TAP `35503B`, so keep the original guard. Verified `git diff --check` and `make NO_COLOR=1`: TAP `35167B` (`-58B` from main `35225B`), BSS guard `0xF0FE < 0xF500` (`1026B` free, `+58B`), overlays unchanged `1808/1846/1547/1992/2001/1733`; `SPECTALK.OVL=12288B`. User hardware test reported normal use OK with no bad behavior noticed.
- Notification pixel stack-clear + faster slide experiment (2026-05-05, branch `codex/notif-stack-clear`, path `C:\tmp\SpecTalkZX-notif-stack-clear`, **HW OK**): tested Gemini's SAFE `_notif_clear()` proposal in isolation. The notification row's 8x32 pixel clear now saves `SP`, disables interrupts, and clears each scanline from `NOTIF_ROW_BASE+32` with 16 `push de` zero writes, then restores `SP` before tail-calling `_fast_fill_attr()` for the 32 attribute bytes. This preserves the slide-in animation and visible output; it only reduces the repeated clear cost inside `_notif_draw()`. - `!save` RX tail-fragment safety fix (2026-05-05): after the large scroll/deferred-wrap commit, rechecked the current save path and tightened only `cmd_save()`. `SPCTLK4` still builds the config in `overlay_slot`/`rx_line` and clears its local ring/parser state, but the resident wrapper now drains UART once after the overlay returns; if any byte arrived during SD I/O, or a partial/overflow state was already live, it re-arms `rx_overflow=1` so the parser discards through the next LF instead of treating a busy-channel tail as a valid IRC line. - Attribute-scroll LDI unroll + blitter setup trim experiment (2026-05-05, branch `codex/scroll-hotpath`, **HW PENDING**): replaced `_scroll_main_zone()`'s 512-byte attribute `LDIR` with an overlap-safe byte-forward 32x`LDI` row body looped 16 times. - Time-source policy implementation (2026-05-04): unified the RTC/SNTP/UDP state around fast startup and a numeric timezone backup. Added resident `sntp_tz_last` (default `+1`) exported to overlays; config now accepts/saves `tzlast=`. Numeric `tz=` and `!tz +/-N` update both the active numeric timezone and `sntp_tz_last`; `tz=rtc` remains RTC opt-in only. If startup RTC seeding fails, `rtc_seed_ovl` now falls back to `sntp_tz_last` instead of hardcoded `+1`, leaving NTP pending for WiFi/AT mode. `!tz rtc` preserves/restores the previous numeric timezone on failure. Normal SPCTLK6 UDP no longer prints technical `NTP ... fail` messages; it fails silently after cleanup, with the `.ntpdate`-exact transport retained. To keep resident growth under the ring-buffer boundary, `tz/tzlast` config parsing is a compact naked ASM helper in `src/spectalk.c`. - Raw UDP NTP HW confirmed (2026-05-04): user confirmed the SPCTLK6 raw UDP fallback now synchronizes the clock on the old AT/divMMC setup, and also resynchronizes correctly after `!tz +3`. Treat the final working stack as `.ntpdate`-exact request (`CIPSEND=60`, `$0B` + 59 zeroes), `+IPD` bytes 40..43, and `cmp4` preserving `HL/DE` before the paired subtract. Keep the temporary failure-stage messages only while further hardware soak is useful; they are now diagnostic, not required for normal UX.
- Raw UDP NTP `NTP bad time` fix (2026-05-04): hardware reported `NTP bad time`, proving DNS/open/send/`+IPD` were already working and the fault was inside timestamp conversion. Root cause: SPCTLK6 `cmp4` decremented `HL/DE` while comparing, then the caller immediately reused `HL` for `sub4`, so subtraction used bytes before the intended 4-byte constant. `.ntpdate` preserves the constant pointer between compare and subtract; SPCTLK6 now does the same by saving/restoring `HL/DE` inside `cmp4`. Verified `make NO_COLOR=1`: TAP `35959B`, BSS guard `0xF4D6 < 0xF500` (`42B` free), overlays `1808/1846/1547/1928/1981/950`; `SPECTALK.OVL=12288B`.
- Raw UDP NTP fallback follow-up (2026-05-04): hardware still held the clock at `00:00`, so `SPCTLK6.OVL` now mirrors the known-working `.ntpdate` binary request exactly: `AT+CIPSEND=60`, first NTP byte `$0B`, then 59 zero bytes. The fallback now prints a compact failure stage (`NTP DNS fail`, `NTP UDP fail`, `NTP send fail`, `NTP no reply`, `NTP bad time`) instead of failing silently, clears `rx_overflow` on overlay exit, and the resident ASM wrapper allows a direct `/server` path to retry after an earlier automatic idle attempt left `sntp_init_sent=3`; automatic idle retries are still suppressed because the main loop only calls the overlay on state `2`. The overlay mirrors the working DivTIESUS `.ntpdate` shape: `AT+CIPDOMAIN="time.google.com"`, `AT+CIPSTART="UDP","ip",123`, `AT+CIPSEND=48`, raw `+IPD` binary read, NTP transmit timestamp conversion from the 2018 epoch constants, numeric `sntp_tz` application, then `time_hour/time_minute/time_second` commit and status redraw. It does not write PCF8563 RTC and does not use `ring_buffer` as RX while overlay code is executing. `SPECTALK.OVL` now packs 6 fixed 2048B blocks; `SPCTLK6.OVL=838B`. - Input cursor CAPS/arrow fix (2026-05-04): hardware still showed the input cursor jumping from the lowercase scanline to the uppercase scanline while browsing command history with cursor keys, and the same happened around word deletion/BREAK. - RX parser phase 1 register-cache (2026-05-04): `_try_read_line_nodrain()` now caches ring tail in `DE` and the live `_rx_line` write pointer in `BC` while consuming a parser pass. It no longer reloads/stores `_rb_tail` and `_rx_pos` for every byte; `_rb_tail` is committed only on valid-line/empty exits, `_rx_pos` is committed only on empty/partial exit, and valid-line/overflow resets are done from the cached pointer state. Overflow contract is preserved: once `BC >= _rx_line + RX_LINE_MAX`, bytes are discarded until LF, `_rx_overflow` remains set, and the next complete/discarded line clears/resets. No UART drain, `/names`, `_frame_wait()`, scheduling, drain-limit, renderer, or telemetry changes. - UART drain phase 1 reverted/rejected (2026-05-04): hardware test of the inline/cache ring push in `_uart_drain_to_buffer()` was catastrophically slower for visible line output. Root cause is the Z80 cost of using `IX/IY` byte registers and prefixed instructions in the per-byte hot loop; the apparent removal of `call _rb_push()` did not pay back the DD/FD-prefix overhead. `_uart_drain_to_buffer()` is restored to the previous `B` counter + `push bc` + direct `uartRead` + `call _rb_push()` shape. Do not revive the `DE=head`, `IY=tail`, `IXL=budget` version. No `/names`, `_frame_wait()`, parser scheduling, drain-limit, or telemetry changes are part of this revert. - IRC count drift investigation, single-channel case (2026-05-03, **no code change / no build**): hardware showed one-channel ChatHispano drift with `!traffic off`: entry `608`, after ~25 min status `638`, immediate manual `/names` `573`. - DivMMC SD I/O prospecting (2026-05-03): reviewed esxDOS/divMMC SD access paths used by fast loaders/demos. Correct boundary: NextZXOS `DISK_FILEMAP`/`DISK_STRMSTART`/`DISK_STRMEND` is still Next-only, but classic esxDOS does expose raw one-sector `DISK_READ`/`DISK_WRITE` plus `F_FSTAT` device info and normal `F_READ`/`F_SEEK`. For SpecTalkZX, safe baseline remains one open `SPECTALK.DAT`, monotonic `F_READ`/bounded `F_SEEK`, sector-sized/aligned packets where RAM permits, and layout/read-ahead improvements. Higher-risk experiment: a probe-gated "turbo DAT" that validates a file-sector map, then uses `DISK_READ` for contiguous 512B packets; reject direct writes or raw LBA reads unless the device, file identity, size, timestamp/checksum, and contiguous/cluster map are validated.

- ABOUT pump hot-loop optimization (2026-05-01, branch `codex/about-parser-anim-experiment`, **HW PENDING**): hardware profiling after the dead-code packet slot showed the remaining `/names` lag is not a memory/scheduler problem. Final diagnostic samples were `/names`: `L=20 T=30 P=61 Y=41` and `L=30 T=40 P=80 Y=50`; idle: `L=3 T=83 P=166 Y=163`. This means the pump is not pathologically stuck on partial lines; the remaining lag is the real cost of parsing IRC lines plus Earth ticks on a 3.5MHz Z80. The debug `ABOUT_PROFILE` build path and `ABP` counters were removed after measurement. Kept optimization: `_about_pump` calls internal divMMC `uartRead` directly (exported from `asm/divmmc_uart.asm`) instead of `_ay_uart_ready` plus `_ay_uart_read` per byte, and caches the next `rx_line` write pointer in `DE` while using `C` for the gap bridge. `rx_pos` is written back only on mid-line return; complete-line paths still set `_rx_last_len`, reset `_rx_pos`, and call the normal parser. Do not cache this in `HL`: `uartRead` uses `HL` to clear `_is_recv`.
- ABOUT dead-code packet slot experiment (2026-05-01, branch `codex/about-parser-anim-experiment`, **HW PENDING**): `SPCTLK2` no longer needs to shrink to `<=1567B` for a tail packet slot. After entry 0 returns, globe ticks read the current 468B Earth packet into this dead code region, leaving `rx_line` free for `_about_pump()` and the normal IRC parser even while `rx_pos > 0`. Verified probe map: `_about_packet_slot=$F6A4`, `_about_packet_slot_end=$F93F` (667B), current packet end `$F878`, live tick/close/seek/apply/draw code stays before the slot, `_earth_frame_buffer=$F99A`, `_earth_attr_buffer=$FBE5`. `_globe_tick_ovl` no longer checks `_rx_pos`; the C scheduler is back to the simple 25Hz gate and no longer uses `about_anim_debt`. `about_close_ovl` stays live outside the dead slot, so exit/N/force_disconnect/read-fail paths can still close DAT safely after ticks overwrite init code. The divMMC path has parked the Next-only `DISK_FILEMAP` experiment: Earth packets are generated-size `481B`, no sector alignment, no footer `F/T` marker, and no `$85/$86/$87` calls in `SPCTLK2`. `!about` no longer arms the fixed `flush_frames=50` post-exit input pause. Before loading ABOUT, `sys_about` processes complete pending `ring_buffer` lines through the normal parser with rendering suppressed. While ABOUT is open, `_overlay_keepalive()` runs before the animation tick with a fixed `224B` byte budget, bridges short UART inter-byte gaps (`D=64`), answers server `PING`, and maintains automatic NAMES state; do not let it drain unbounded or the animation stops during large `/names` bursts. Fixed a concrete ABOUT NAMES bug where the scanner recognized `353` but not `366`, so the status bar could never commit/update inside ABOUT. This branch is intentionally frozen for comparison with the parser-pump experiment.
- ABOUT DISK_FILEMAP streaming prototype (2026-04-30, parked for Next): branch `codex/about-disk-filemap-streaming` / safety patch `.codex-safety/about-disk-filemap-current.patch` preserves the experimental turbo path. Keep its 512B sector padding, `EARTH_STREAM_*` constants, footer `F/T` marker, and NextZXOS `$85/$86/$87` calls out of the divMMC stabilization branch until a separate Next-specific hardware pass.
- ABOUT automatic NAMES state-drain (2026-04-30, **HW PENDING**): `_overlay_keepalive()` now does a minimal streaming protocol drain while ABOUT owns `ring_buffer`. It still stores only a capped PING line in `temp_input`, but it counts whitespace-delimited tokens for each incoming line using existing RX state (`rx_last_len` as token count, `rx_overflow` as the current-token flag). On automatic `353`, it adds `tokens - 5` to `names_count_acc` and resets `names_timeout_frames`; on `366`, it closes `names_pending`, clears `counting_new_users`, writes `names_count_acc` into `cur_chan_ptr->user_count`, and marks `status_bar_dirty`, so the status bar can refresh while still inside ABOUT. This intentionally handles automatic JOIN/NAMES only; it does not render or complete manual `/names` pagination inside ABOUT. To fit, ABOUT PONG consumption was dropped because post-exit `about_keepalive_rebaseline()` already clears stale local PING state; server `PING` replies remain.
- ABOUT post-exit keepalive + theme-adaptive Earth fix (2026-04-30, updated 2026-05-01, **HW PENDING**): leaving ABOUT closes DAT, then rebaselines local keepalive state (`server_silence_frames`, `keepalive_ping_sent`, `keepalive_timeout`, `lagmeter_counter`) before normal IRC parsing resumes; this prevents a lost/stale pre-ABOUT PONG from expiring immediately after the overlay and producing false `Connection timeout (no response)`. The later `flush_frames=50` quiet drain has been removed because it blocked input and still allowed confusing post-exit bursts. ABOUT rows clear with `TATTR_MAIN_BG`; separator uses `TATTR_MSG_TOPIC`; logo is white only in theme 1 and `TATTR_MSG_NICK` otherwise; Ikkle text uses fixed yellow/white only in theme 1 and theme attrs in other themes. Earth attribute rendering merges generated ink/BRIGHT with the active theme PAPER; theme 2 maps Earth ink to green and keeps generated BRIGHT for shading, while theme 3 keeps its own background instead of forcing black.
- Double-height banner bright split restored (2026-04-30, **HW PENDING**): `_draw_big_char()` now writes the upper attribute row as `_g_ps64_attr | 0x40` and the lower row as `_g_ps64_attr & 0xBF`, preserving theme ink/paper while forcing BRIGHT 1 on top and BRIGHT 0 on bottom. This fixes the regression where `print_big_str()` overwrote the banner/header pre-clears with the same attribute on both rows. Cost: `+4B` resident/TAP (`35813B -> 35817B`) and BSS gap `125B -> 121B`; overlays unchanged.
- SPCTLK2 `!about` BASIC exit fix (2026-04-30, **HW PENDING**): hardware reported immediate return to BASIC with `SIN SENTIDO EN BASIC, 10:3` after the ASM tick refactor. Root cause was a generated-layout mismatch: `tools/bpe_build.py` now emits `Earth 12703B (481B packets), help @13672`, so `EARTH_PACKET_SIZE=481` and `EARTH_DELTA_OFFSET=2128`, but `overlay/overlay_entry2.asm` still hardcoded the old `512` packet and `1847` offset from an earlier DAT layout. The first `F_READ` consumed 31 bytes of the next packet; later ticks parsed bogus `frame_delta_len` and could apply deltas from outside the valid `overlay_slot` packet, corrupting memory/return state. Fixed by setting the ASM DEFCs to `481/2128` and extending `tools/bpe_build.py` to patch `overlay_entry2.asm` from the same `earth_offsets` used for `overlay_api.h`; `Makefile` now tracks `overlay_entry2.asm` in BPE inputs and saves/restores it with the other BPE-patched sources. Verified twice with `make NO_COLOR=1`: `35733B` trimmed / `35813B` TAP / `125B` BSS gap; SPCTLK2 remains `1809B`.
- SPCTLK2 surgical refactor (2026-04-30, **HW PENDING**): three-rule cirurgical pass on the about overlay. (1) Removed redundant `about_dat_open` static — the system already knows the DAT is open through `esx_handle != 0`. (2) Eradicated the helpers `dat_open_at`, `dat_read`, and `reset_delta_stream`, which forced SDCC to spend prologue/epilogue (IX frame) bytes on each call; replaced with a `READ_DAT(buf,sz)` macro that inlines the three-line read+check pattern. (3) Moved `globe_tick_ovl` from C into native ASM in `overlay_entry2.asm`, with `_earth_ready` and `_frame_idx` becoming PUBLIC ASM bytes; the new ASM tick uses `add hl, de` for pointer arithmetic and tail-jumps to `_about_close_ovl` on read/seek failure and to `_earth_draw_frame` on success. SPCTLK2: 1917B -> 1809B (-108B; margin 131B -> 239B). Resident TAP unchanged (overlay internal). Needs HW test of `!about` with active globe rotation, N-to-WhatsNew transition, and exit-via-any-key path.
- `cmd_save` caller-side gate removed (2026-04-30): now that `save_config_ovl` captures `old_rx_pos` at entry and conditionally raises `rx_overflow`, the residual `had_partial = rx_pos` capture and `if (!had_partial) rx_overflow = 0` clear in `cmd_save` are redundant. Removed both, leaving the 3-line caller `(void)args; snapshot_autojoin_channels(); overlay_exec(3, 1);`. SPCTLK4 unchanged at 1954B; resident shrunk by 12B (`35825B` -> `35813B` TAP, `113B` -> `125B` BSS gap).
- SPCTLK4 Gemini suggestions follow-up (2026-04-30): three external proposals applied verbatim. (1) Pointer arithmetic in `_cfg_put_autojoin` already unified earlier in this session. (2) `ovl4_put_a_hl` rewritten to preserve BC instead of DE so callers like `_cfg_put` no longer pay an external push/pop DE pair around each call; same 20B function size, register-preservation contract changed. (3) `save_config_ovl` now captures `old_rx_pos` at entry and only sets `rx_overflow=1` if there was a real RX fragment in flight, so the discard rule lives inside the overlay rather than depending on the caller. Net SPCTLK4: 1937B -> 1954B (+17B from suggestion 3 capture/conditional, suggestion 2 neutral by design as predicted). The caller-side gate in `cmd_save` (`if (!had_partial) rx_overflow = 0`) is now redundant but kept until evaluation against `overlay-save-fragment-discard.md`.
- SPCTLK4 `_cfg_put_autojoin` pointer arithmetic shrink (2026-04-30): replaced both byte-wise pointer adds (`ld a,l / add a,N / ld l,a / jr nc / inc h`) with `ld de,N / add hl,de` for the +30 (CH_FLAGS_OFF) and +32 (CH_SIZE) advances inside the channels loop. Matches the pattern already used in `_cfg_put_friends` (+18) and `_cfg_put_ignores` (+16). DE is dead at both sites in the loop. Saves 6B in SPCTLK4 (1943B -> 1937B). TAP unchanged (overlay internal). Suggestion 2 (BC vs DE in `ovl4_put_a_hl`) was rejected after byte counting: same 20B function size, only shifts which register the function preserves; would force DE-using callers like `_cfg_put` to add their own push/pop. Suggestion 3 (encapsulate RX discard inside save_config_ovl) was net-zero on bytes; kept current caller-side gate per `overlay-save-fragment-discard.md`.
- Current `shrink-z80 scan` follow-up (2026-04-30): two groups of SAFE optimizations applied without touching user-visible strings, commands, or OVL2/OVL4 (frozen pending HW for `!about`/`!tz`). Resident group: drop the redundant pre-guard around the main-loop `sntp_init()` call (the naked-ASM function already has the same three early-rets); drop the unreachable `sntp_tz != TZ_RTC` check inside the SNTP query block (impossible state when `sntp_init_sent==1`); drop the `if (!sntp_init_sent)` wrapper in `cmd_connect` (sntp_init() is self-guarded); drop the 2nd-letter null check in `overlay_keepalive` ASM (the trailing `cp 'I'/'O'` filter handles `B=0`). SPCTLK5 group: merged `rtc_validate_msdos`+`rtc_commit_msdos` into a single-pass `rtc_decode_msdos` (no push/pop BC/DE around the call, no separate commit pass); merged `i2c_nack`/`i2c_ack` with shared `i2c_clock_pulse` using `set 1,d`/`res 1,d` to toggle SCL while preserving SDA; factored a shared `rtc_esx_epilogue` between `rtc_try_drvapi` and `rtc_try_getdate`; merged the `tz_print_numeric` sign branches by hoisting `ld l,'+'` before `jp p` (since `ld r,n` preserves flags); reordered `tz_show_current` before `tz_suffix_none` so the suffix=none path falls through to `tz_print_numeric`; unified `pcf_fail` with `bcd_fail`; replaced the two-byte `_tick_accum` clears with `ld (_tick_accum),hl`; removed a dead `ld c,a` in `_tz_cmd_ovl`. Total recovery: `-35B` TAP/resident (`+35B` BSS gap from `78B` to `113B`) and `-65B` SPCTLK5 (from `2046B` to `1981B`, margin from 2B to 67B). All four audit findings (F01 EI, F02 parser, F03 margin, F04 anim_gate static) remain in place.
- Current `audit-z80 full` follow-up (2026-04-30): four findings fixed without touching user-visible strings or commands. F01: PCF8563 I2C path in `rtc_seed_ovl.asm` now restores interrupts with `ei` after `i2c_stop` before `pcf_validate_commit`, closing the DI leak that previously persisted from I2C bit-bang through overlay return into the next `frame_wait`. F02: `cfg_apply()` `tz=` parser now requires the two-character `rt` prefix instead of any `r`-prefixed value, so `tz=random` or `tz=reset` no longer silently activate RTC mode. F04: main-loop `about_anim_gate` toggle is now `static` so its 25 Hz globe-tick alternation persists if anything reorders/restructures the enclosing `while(1)` block. ASM shrink in `_tz_cmd_ovl` collapses the sign apply to `dec b / jr nz / cpl / inc a` (-2B SPCTLK5), funding the `+1B` `ei`. Cost vs prior baseline (`35837B` TAP / `102B` gap): `+23B` TAP/resident, `-24B` BSS gap. SPCTLK5 stays under budget at `2046/2048`.
- Current ABOUT server-timeout fix (2026-04-30): hardware showed server-side `Closing Link ... (Ping timeout: 120 seconds)` after staying in `!about`, plus visible backlog dump on exit. Root causes: `_overlay_keepalive()` returned on the first empty UART-ready check, so at 115200 baud it could drain too slowly and leave server `PING` buried behind channel traffic; and the ABOUT exit path set `flush_frames=15` but still fell through to normal `process_irc_data()` in the same frame with `overlay_mode=0`, rendering the backlog before the quiet drain started. Fixes: `_overlay_keepalive()` now polls through short inter-byte gaps (`D=64`) before returning, and the ABOUT key-exit path `continue`s immediately after arming the silent drain. Build cost versus prior `!tz` C fix: `+8B` TAP/resident, BSS gap `110B -> 102B`.
- Current `!tz` hardware regression fix (2026-04-30): the resident `cmd_tz()` naked ASM wrapper was replaced with a normal C wrapper after hardware kept reporting `Overlay load failed`. The C path snapshots `rx_pos`, dispatches lowercase `rtc` to `SPCTLK5.OVL` entry 2, copies every other argument into `overlay_slot` with `st_copy_n(..., 8)`, and dispatches numeric/show/range handling to `SPCTLK5.OVL` entry 3. This spends `+30B` resident/TAP versus the prior build (`35799B -> 35829B`) and leaves `110B` BSS gap, but removes the hand-built `overlay_exec` parameter frame from this command. `SPECTALK.OVL` table check: SPCTLK5 `count=4`, entry 3 address `$F50A`.
- Current overlay/keepalive regression fix (2026-04-30): reverted the temporary numeric `!tz` rebalance, returning `_tz_cmd_ovl` to `SPCTLK5.OVL` entry 3 and changing the naked dispatcher literal back to `overlay_exec(4,3)`. The SPCTLK3 move had measured well locally but produced hardware `Overlay load failed` reports for `!tz`, likely because TAP/OVL deployment can get out of sync. Also changed the main keepalive block so `OVERLAY_ABOUT` no longer starts new client-originated keepalive/lag PINGs or expires a pending local PING while normal IRC parsing is paused; `_overlay_keepalive()` still consumes PONG and answers server PING from `temp_input`. This fixes the false `Connection timeout (no response)` auto-exit during long `!about` sessions. New build is `35719B` trimmed / `35799B` TAP / `140B` BSS gap.
- Current shrink pass over about/RTC/SNTP (2026-04-30): `shrink-z80` scan recovered `144B` trimmed/TAP and `+145B` BSS gap versus the post-RTC/status-restored peak (`35825B` trimmed / `35905B` TAP / `33B` gap). Accepted safe wins: removed the separate resident RTC-available byte and uses `sntp_tz==TZ_RTC` as the only RTC state, moved `overlay_keepalive()` from C to resident ASM using `temp_input` and `_rx_pos_reset`, rewrote the `!tz` dispatcher as naked ASM, rewrote `sntp_init()`/`sntp_query_time()` as naked ASM, shortened safe overlay loader/earth renderer long jumps, and kept user-visible `!status` labels intact.
- Current RTC/NTP time-source pass (2026-04-30): RTC is optional and transaccional. `sntp_tz=TZ_RTC(127)` is the saved/user-selected RTC mode; numeric `sntp_tz` keeps the SNTP/timezone path. Config accepts and saves `tz=rtc`; `!tz rtc` runs `SPCTLK5.OVL` entry 2, tries RTC immediately, updates `time_hour/time_minute/time_second` only after full validation, clears SNTP flags, and prints `tz=RTC` on success, or prints `No RTC` and restores the previous timezone without touching the current clock on failure. Numeric `!tz` runs as `SPCTLK5.OVL` entry 3: from RTC it exits RTC without adjusting the displayed hour, clears `sntp_init_sent/sntp_waiting/sntp_queried` to force fresh SNTP, and prints `tz=+N sync` in `STATE_WIFI_OK` or `tz=+N later` while offline/TCP/IRC; numeric-to-numeric changes still adjust `time_hour` by timezone delta and mark SNTP pending. Startup only probes RTC when `tz=rtc` was loaded; if startup RTC seed fails, the seed overlay clears RTC mode back to numeric `sntp_tz=1`. The main loop starts pending SNTP only while `STATE_WIFI_OK`; `/server` also re-runs `sntp_init()` after `force_disconnect()` if a TZ change cleared the SNTP config before the connect path reaches `CIPSTART`. The cold RTC reader remains in `SPCTLK5.OVL` entry 1: documented esxDOS/Next `M_DRVAPI ($92)` with `C=0/B=0`, then `M_GETDATE ($8e)`, then direct PCF8563 fallback through ZX-Uno-style `FC3B/FD3B`. All sources validate date/time before acceptance (`2024..2035`, month/day/hour/min/sec ranges). DivTIESUS hardware confirmation: after `.ntpdate +2` followed by a real power-cycle, direct PCF8563 read works with SDA input mask `80`; do not apply a second timezone correction on the PCF path. The temporary RTC diagnostic display and `rtc_diag[19]` buffer were removed after hardware confirmation.
- Current GloboTerraqueoZX `!about` integration (2026-04-30): branch `codex/about-earth-overlay` replaces the old procedural `!about` globe with the 24-frame bitmap Earth package streamed from `SPECTALK.DAT`. Current generated asset pass uses `TEMPORAL_HYSTERESIS=0.025` and reversed playback phases `0,-15,-30...` so the globe rotates west-to-east like Earth; assets live under `release/about_earth/`; `tools/about_earth_polish.py` post-processes the compact bitmap frames by filling single black pinholes fully surrounded by lit pixels, leaving attributes/colors unchanged; `tools/bpe_build.py` emits `font+themes+BPE dict + Earth block + help` and patches generated `EARTH_*_OFFSET/SIZE`, `EARTH_PACKET_SIZE`, plus `BPE_HELP_OFFSET`. SPCTLK2 is now about-only with renderer/buffers, fixed generated-size `overlay_slot` delta packets (`481B` in the current pass), an Ikkle info renderer, and `about_close_ovl`; `!config` moved to new `SPCTLK5.OVL`. The layout keeps normal banner rows 0..1, blank row 2, globe rows 3..12, 176x24 logo rows 13..15, Ikkle rows 16..17, Ikkle footer row 20, status/input rows 21..23. About exit/N/keepalive-timeout paths call the close entry before replacing or leaving the overlay. Hardware feedback follow-ups restored the row-2 banner separator, adapted about rows/separator/logo/text/Earth attrs to active themes while keeping theme 1's deliberate black/multicolor identity, applies bitmap+attribute deltas before drawing each animation tick, preserves `IX` across the public Earth draw entry used by `overlay_call`, keeps the Ikkle physical attribute column across glyph row loops, nudges the two text rows right, uses the normal notification/Ikkle footer, applies a table mask to fixed lower-right edge sparkles after each Earth draw, moves the about keepalive scanner from aliased `rx_line` to `temp_input`, keeps the status-bar clock ticking during overlays with the minute/hour wrap applied before drawing, reduces globe animation from four DAT reads per visual tick to one generated-size read, runs the globe tick every other main-loop frame to reduce SD I/O and perceived shimmer, uses esxDOS `F_SEEK` to rewind the cyclic delta stream instead of closing/reopening/skipping from the start of `SPECTALK.DAT`, reduces logo startup I/O from 24 row reads to two reads, and calls globe ticks through `overlay_call_timed()`, which temporarily sets `IY=0x5C3A` and enables IM1 interrupts only during the about animation entry so ROM `FRAMES` advances during long DAT/draw work. The prior I/O batching alone was not enough to prevent visible clock drift.
- Current SS+arrow input polish (2026-04-29): raw `key_ss_arrow()` now recognizes `SS+UP` and `SS+DOWN` in addition to `SS+LEFT/RIGHT/BACKSPACE`. `SS+UP` jumps to input start, `SS+DOWN` jumps to input end, and the SS word navigation/delete path now calls `key_click()` on actual repeat ticks so click feedback matches normal key input. Follow-up fixed `_input_word_right()` after HW/user report: adding `_input_line_start` had accidentally broken the old fall-through into `wm_apply`; `_input_word_right()` now jumps explicitly to `wm_apply` after `wb_right`. - Current help footer redraw polish (2026-04-29): SPCTLK1 help now draws `ANY KEY: NEXT / BREAK: EXIT` only on page 0. - Current status-bar bounded render fix (2026-04-29): `draw_status_bar_real()` now uses `print_status_left54_fast(sb_left_part)` instead of full-row `_print_line64_fast()`. Root cause of right-side flicker: the left status rebuild was blank-padding all 64 logical columns, briefly erasing the clock and connection indicator before C repainted them. The new ASM wrapper sets an optional `_print_line64_fast()` pair limit of 27 physical bytes (logical cols `0..53`), so cols `54..63` remain owned by `draw_clock()`/`draw_indicator()`. Promoted normal build passes at `35684B` trimmed / `35764B` TAP / `175B` free; overlays `2025/2037/1500/1885`.
- Current unpacked-font planning note (2026-04-29): creating a fifth overlay is plausible for cold code, but safe local-management candidates alone probably do not free enough resident space for `FONT_L/FONT_R`. The promising package is local management (`cmd_ignore/cmd_friend`) plus cold IRC send-only commands (`cmd_search`, `cmd_topic`, `cmd_mode`, `cmd_kick`, `cmd_whois/list/who`), roughly `1327B` gross and estimated `~950..1075B` net after wrappers if kept tight. This likely funds the unpacked-DAT path; keeping packed font data as well remains borderline unless another small cluster moves too. Do not move `/server`/connect or any UART-waiting command to an overlay because overlay code executes from `_ring_buffer`.
- Current raw6 font renderer (2026-04-29): promoted to default. The BPE/DAT build always replaces `[10B LUT]+[288B packed glyphs]` with `96*6=576B` raw glyph rows already expanded through the old LUT, keeps themes after the font block, and moves help/BPE offsets from `373+dict` to `651+dict`. `unpack_glyph()` is now pointer math into `font64_raw6`; renderers loop over 6 glyph rows and explicitly blank the bottom padding scanline. Important contract: `_print_line64_fast()` must `INC H` after writing the raw6 bottom padding so its common pair-advance contract still sees `HL` one character cell below the rendered byte (`H += 8`).
- Current stack-blit scroll path (2026-04-29): promoted to default for the 224-byte block-3 bitmap copy inside `_scroll_main_zone()`. The original external variant with `C` as loop counter was rejected because `POP BC` destroys `C`; the accepted integrated variant uses `IXL` and preserves `IX` inside `_scroll_stack_blit_224` so the public `_scroll_main_zone()` ABI does not inherit an index-register clobber. It uses `DI` while hijacking `SP` but deliberately does not `EI`; it returns with interrupts still disabled, matching normal mainline expectations. Destination SMC updates only the low operand byte because block 3's destination top advances `0x4810..0x48E0` and never crosses page before the final unused update.
- Current `50_main_output.asm` output-layout micro pass (2026-04-29): accepted all three safe items from the latest external output-focused pass after checking stack shape. `_main_print()` now places `mp_bpe_slow` directly on the over-64-character fallback path, sharing the one `POP HL` and falling through to `mp_slow` instead of branching from a separate BPE block. `_main_print_wrapped_ram()` replaces both post-newline pagination-cancel jumps to `mpwr_abort` with direct `RET Z`; in both cases all temporary segment stack state has already been restored. `_main_print_time_prefix()` handles timestamp-off inline by storing `_wrap_indent=0` while `A` is already zero, removing the old `mptp_off/mptp_ret` tail. Full `make NO_COLOR=1` passes at `35616B` trimmed / `35696B` TAP / `518B` free (`BSS_END_tail=$F2FA`, `_ring_buffer=$F500`); overlays remain `2019/2037/1500/1885`. - Current `30_rendering.asm` 64-col render micro pass (2026-04-29): accepted all five safe items from the latest external render-focused pass after checking the real hot paths. `_print_str64_char()` now routes space/control/high bytes directly to a relocated `p64_space_path` after the normal attr-return block, keeping the explicit nibble clear path while letting printable `33..127` fall through to glyph rendering without the old `ld a,32 / cp 32` validation chain. `p64_get_scr_base()` cache miss saves row `A` in `B` instead of `PUSH AF/POP AF`, saving cycles with no byte delta; `_compute_screen_base()` does not touch `B`. `unpack_glyph()` rereads the compressed byte from `DE` for the low nibble instead of saving it in `C`, saving one byte and one T-state per packed byte. `_put_char64_input_cached()` forms `$5AC0/$5AE0` attrs with `add a,0xC0` instead of `set 7,l / set 6,l`. `_draw_cursor_underline()` defaults to the even-column masks and patches the odd case with `ld d,b / ld b,0xF0`. - Current `40_text_numeric_screen.asm` scroll/string micro pass (2026-04-29): accepted all five safe items from the latest external scroll-focused pass after checking the real code. `_scroll_main_zone()` now scans bitmap scanlines through `IYL=7..0` and exits with `DEC IYL / JP P`, keeping the copied regions identical while removing the old `LD A,IYL / CP 8` loop check. `_reapply_screen_attributes()` tail-jumps to `_set_sbd()` after setting `_force_status_redraw`. `_st_stristr()` now returns early with `RET Z` for NULL/empty needle after the cdecl stack has already been restored, removing the local `sstr_ret_hay` block. `_strip_irc_codes()` inlines the four IRC color digit checks and removes the now single-use `strip_is_digit` helper. `_st_stricmp()` returns directly from the diff path instead of jumping to a shared one-byte epilogue. - Current `80_ui_runtime.asm` micro pass (2026-04-28): accepted the safe subset of the latest external 80-file pass after checking input-buffer and keyboard contracts. `_set_nick_color()` now computes `(hash % 6) + 1` with subtract-until-underflow plus `add a,7`, preserving the old 1..6 ink range. `_in_inkey()` tail-merges the shifted-table `ADD HL,DE`. `_key_ss_arrow()` now cascades `L=1/2/3` with conditional returns for SS+LEFT/RIGHT/BACKSPACE, keeping `L=0` for no combo. `wb_left_clean()` uses `CPDR` for the backward non-space scan; the `inc c` after a match is required because `CPDR` decrements `BC` after comparing. `wb_right()` now trusts the guaranteed NUL terminator in `_line_buffer` instead of reloading `_line_len` as a loop limit. - Current MODE notification routing (2026-04-28): general channel MODE messages now honor `!notif`. The old non-ban branch in `h_mode()` printed `nick sets mode +x on #channel` directly with `main_puts2()/main_print()`, bypassing ikkle notifications. It now builds the same exact text with the existing `nb_init()/nb()/NB_END()` chain and calls `notify(temp_input, ATTR_MSG_SYS)`, so `!notif 1` routes it to the footer and `!notif 0` falls back to classic main-area output through `notify()`. - Current `/names` cancel/drain root fix (2026-04-28): user HW test showed the previous narrow `><` suppression still let queued NAMES payload render after `Cancelled`. Root cause: `show_names_list` was being used both as "render the list" and "manual NAMES owns the incoming 353/366 stream"; `cancel_search_state()` cleared it, so pending `353` chunks stopped being centrally filtered. Final model: `show_names_list` remains set until matching `366` or timeout, while `pagination_active` alone controls whether the list is rendered. After BREAK or incomplete close, `pagination_active=0`; dispatcher still allows only `353/366/PING/PONG`, and `h_numeric_353()` silently consumes matching chunks until `366` clears the NAMES state. - Current `irc_handlers.c` Gemini pass (2026-04-28): applied the measured safe parser subset. Added local `ST_NAKED` ASM `split_next_param()` to specialize the IRC parser's space split: it NUL-terminates the current token at the first space, skips following spaces, and returns the next token pointer; `parse_irc_message()` now uses it for IRCv3 tags, prefix-to-command split, and command-to-params split, removing the local `strchr()+skip_spaces()` and `skip_to()+skip_spaces()` overhead on that hot path. Rejected generic `call %1%2 / ret -> jp %1%2` copt because z88dk copt rejects an unconstrained end-of-line capture (`input pattern %n% is not allowed`); exact-symbol tail-call rules would need generated ASM proof. `is_ignored` was already resident ASM in `50_main_output.asm`, so the CPIR rewrite is not an `irc_handlers.c` C win and would need a separate case-insensitive ASM prototype. - Current CRT/buffer proposal triage (2026-04-28): reviewed the latest external "heavy artillery" pass. The CRT override idea is already mostly present in the build contract: `CLIB_MALLOC_HEAP_SIZE=0`, `CLIB_STDIO_HEAP_SIZE=0`, `CRT_ENABLE_STDIO=0`, `-startup=31`, and adding `CRT_ENABLE_COMMANDLINE=0` measured no TAP/BSS delta (`35922B`, `BSS_END_tail=$F3DC`). Reject `REGISTER_SP=0xFFFF`: the current fixed stack top is deliberately below the UDG-backed high-RAM aliases (`_friend_nicks=$FF58`, `_away_message=$FFB2`, `_names_target_channel=$FFD2`), so `$FFFF` would stack over live data. Do not set `CRT_INITIALIZE_BSS=0` without a z88dk CRT proof; resident startup already uses a custom `code_crt_init` BSS clear with a size-one `LDIR` guard. The suggested `pass_buffer` alias is stale: no `pass_buffer` exists, UDG high RAM is fully allocated, and `search_pattern`/`autojoin_channels` have intentionally different lifetimes because `autojoin_channels` must survive scratch use of `search_pattern` before restored-session JOIN replay. A `ui_msg(index)` vector wrapper is only worth prototyping for repeated messages; for one-off strings the 2-byte table entry plus dispatcher eats the callsite pointer saving. - Current demoscene proposal follow-up (2026-04-28): accepted two proven local wins from the latest external pass. `_st_strlen()` in `40_text_numeric_screen.asm` now keeps the existing 256-byte safety bound but derives the 0..255 length from `C` after `CPIR` (`CPL`) instead of saving the start pointer in `DE` and doing 16-bit subtraction; `H` is cleared with `LD H,B` because bounded `CPIR` always leaves `B=0`. `text_shift_right()` and `text_shift_left()` in `60_protocol_storage.asm` dropped redundant `PUSH IY`/`POP IY`; neither `LDDR` nor `LDIR` touches `IY`. Rejected the unbounded `BC=0` strlen form because a missing NUL would scan 64K instead of capping at 255. Rejected the proposed `_st_stricmp_asm_fast` as a mainline change for now because adding a new entry/exit around the current IX-based routine is not an obvious net resident-byte win without a measured prototype. Rejected page-aligning `_channels`: current `_channels=$ED8E`, aligning would burn scarce BSS slack, and the proposed low-byte-only rotate math fails for slots 8 and 9 because `ChannelInfo[10]` crosses a 256-byte page. The dither "bug" is stale: current `dbd_scanline` already writes `00` before `SCF/RLA`, producing `00,01,03,07,0F,1F,3F,7F`. Full `make NO_COLOR=1` passes at `35842B` trimmed / `35922B` TAP / `292B` free (`BSS_END_tail=$F3DC`, `_ring_buffer=$F500`); overlays remain `2019/2037/1500/1885`.
- Current C/ASM bridge proposal triage (2026-04-28): reviewed the follow-up Gemini proposals. Reject a permanent hardware context in alternate registers: this codebase already uses `EXX` for cdecl cleanup return-address shims and glyph lookup scratch, and `EX AF,AF'` in input/autojoin helpers, so global `BC'/DE'/HL'` state would be silently clobbered unless many current wins were rewritten. Mailbox/globals are valid only as measured per-callsite optimizations; the project already uses parser globals in `irc_handlers.c` and `g_ps64_*` render state, but `$5BC0` is transient glyph/BPE scratch and not safe as a generic mailbox. Dense ASM jump tables only make sense for dense ids; IRC numerics and command hashes are sparse, and user command dispatch is string lookup plus function pointer table, so a pure `cmd_id*2` table would waste memory or miss the real cost. New `copt` rules must prove A/register liveness; broad `ld a,(hl) / ld r,a / ld rr,0` rewrites are unsafe if `A` is still live, and the `channels[].flags` base+offset case is already handled by existing helper rules.
- Current aggressive Z80 proposal triage (2026-04-28): reviewed the external Gemini byte/T-state ideas against the actual SpecTalkZX target. Keep byte-skipper opcode overlap and asymmetric tail merging as local hand-ASM options only when flags, stack shape, and fall-through labels are proven. Reject generic UART/buffer stack hijacking outside already-proven startup/screen-clear style cases; `POP` does not read UART streams and runtime SP theft conflicts with C stack/IM1/ROM/esxDOS contracts. Reject RST-slot repurposing for the current 48K/divMMC target because low memory is ROM/esxDOS/IM1 territory (`RST 8` is esxDOS, `$0038` is ROM IM1). Treat SMC state operands as experimental; with shared flags such as `_is_recv`, multiple read sites make coherent operand updates larger and riskier than the one-byte BSS saving. Custom copt remains the best real path, but this project already uses `src\spectalk_copt.rul` through z88dk `-custom-copt-rules`, so new peepholes must match z88dk syntax and prove A/register liveness plus a clean `make`.

- Current external `divmmc_uart.asm` holistic audit follow-up (2026-04-26): `make` passes at `35688B` trimmed / `35768B` TAP / `446B` BSS slack; overlays remain `SPCTLK1/2/3/4 = 2019/2037/1853/2041`. Accepted all three safe UART shrinks: `_ay_uart_send()` no longer reloads `BC=ZXUNO_REG` after the RX-ready probe because `inc b` already leaves `BC=$FD3B` and the `_is_recv` store does not touch `BC`; `_ay_uart_init()` uses `dec b` to return from register port `$FD3B` to address port `$FC3B` before selecting `UART_DATA_REG`; and `uartRead_do_read` clears `_is_recv` through `ld hl,_is_recv / ld (hl),0`, preserving the received byte in `A` without the old `E` shuttle. Current map anchors after this pass: `_ay_uart_send=$C38A`, `_ay_uart_ready=$C3AC`, `_ay_uart_read=$C3C4`, `_is_recv=$F07D`, `_font_lut=$F086`, and `u8a_tbl_c0=$D3C9`.
- Current external `overlay_loader.asm` audit follow-up (2026-04-26): `make` passes at `35694B` trimmed / `35774B` TAP / `440B` BSS slack; overlays remain `SPCTLK1/2/3/4 = 2019/2037/1853/2041`. Accepted the safe loader shrinks: `ovl_skip` no longer rewrites `_esx_count=2048` after every `_esx_fread()` because `_esx_fread()` only reads `_esx_count` into `BC` and writes `_esx_result`; the post-load RX cleanup now collapses `rb_tail = rb_head` immediately and folds the three overflow predicates through `A` while preserving the loaded entry pointer on the stack; both `_overlay_exec` cleanup exits remove the two callee params with `pop bc` instead of two `inc sp`; and `_overlay_call` now pops the validated entry pointer directly into `HL` before `jp (hl)`.
